stroke-linejoin="round"></path></g></svg>Share</button></span></div></div></div></div></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We’ve trained a large-scale unsupervised language model which generates coherent paragraphs of text, achieves state-of-the-art performance on many language modeling benchmarks, and performs rudimentary reading comprehension, machine translation, question answering, and summarization—all without task-specific training.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Our model, called GPT‑2 (a successor to </span><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" href="/index/language-unsupervised/"><span>GPT</span>⁠</a><span>), was trained simply to predict the next word in 40GB of Internet text. Due to our concerns about malicious applications of the technology, we are not releasing the trained model. As an experiment in responsible disclosure, we are instead releasing a much </span><a href="https://github.com/openai/gpt-2" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>smaller model</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> for researchers to experiment with, as well as a </span><a href="https://cdn.openai.com/better-language-models/language_models_are_unsupervised_multitask_learners.pdf" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" referrerPolicy="no-referrer-when-downgrade"><span>technical paper</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>GPT‑2 is a large </span><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/1706.03762" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>transformer</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>-based language model with 1.5 billion parameters, trained on a dataset</span><sup><span id="citation-top-A"><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-primary-100 hover:text-primary-60 text-xs no-underline" href="#citation-bottom-A">A</a></span></sup><span> of 8 million web pages. GPT‑2 is trained with a simple objective: predict the next word, given all of the previous words within some text. The diversity of the dataset causes this simple goal to contain naturally occurring demonstrations of many tasks across diverse domains. GPT‑2 is a direct scale-up of GPT, with more than 10X the parameters and trained on more than 10X the amount of data.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>GPT‑2 displays a broad set of capabilities, including the ability to generate conditional synthetic text samples of unprecedented quality, where we prime the model with an input and have it generate a lengthy continuation. In addition, GPT‑2 outperforms other language models trained on specific domains (like Wikipedia, news, or books) without needing to use these domain-specific training datasets. On language tasks like question answering, reading comprehension, summarization, and translation, GPT‑2 begins to learn these tasks from the raw text, using no task-specific training data. While scores on these downstream tasks are far from state-of-the-art, they suggest that the tasks can benefit from unsupervised techniques, given sufficient (unlabeled) data and compute.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="samples"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Samples</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>GPT‑2 generates synthetic text samples in response to the model being primed with an arbitrary input. The model is chameleon-like—it adapts to the style and content of the conditioning text. This allows the user to generate realistic and coherent continuations about a topic of their choosing, as seen by the following select samples.</span><sup><span id="citation-top-B"><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-primary-100 hover:text-primary-60 text-xs no-underline" href="#citation-bottom-B">B</a></span></sup></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><section class="theme-light-gray @container grid grid-cols-12 w-full max-w-container max-w-[108rem]"><div class="col-span-12"><div role="status" class="max-w-container flex h-32 max-w-sm animate-pulse items-center justify-center rounded-lg bg-gray-300 dark:bg-gray-700"><span>Loading...</span></div></div></section><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>As the above samples show, our model is capable of generating samples from a variety of prompts that feel close to human quality and show coherence over a page or more of text. Nevertheless, we have observed various failure modes, such as repetitive text, world modeling failures (e.g., the model sometimes writes about </span><i><span>fires happening under water</span></i><span>), and unnatural topic switching. Exploring these types of weaknesses of language models is an </span><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/1601.04811" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>active</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> </span><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/1510.03055" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>area</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> of </span><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/1701.03185" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>research</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> in the natural language processing community.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Overall, we find that it takes a few tries to get a good sample, with the number of tries depending on how familiar the model is with the context. When prompted with topics that are highly represented in the data (Brexit, Miley Cyrus, Lord of the Rings, and so on), it seems to be capable of generating reasonable samples about 50% of the time. The opposite is also true: on highly technical or esoteric types of content, the model can perform poorly. Fine-tuning offers the potential for even more detailed control over generated samples—for example, we can fine-tune GPT‑2 on the Amazon Reviews dataset and use this to let us write reviews conditioned on things like star rating and category.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>These samples have substantial policy implications: large language models are becoming increasingly easy to steer towards scalable, customized, coherent text generation, which in turn could be used in a number of beneficial as well as malicious ways. We’ll discuss these implications below in more detail, and outline a publication experiment we are taking in light of such considerations.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="zero-shot"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Zero-shot</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>GPT‑2 achieves state-of-the-art scores on a variety of domain-specific language modeling tasks. Our model is not trained on any of the data specific to any of these tasks and is only evaluated on them as a final test; this is known as the “zero-shot” setting. GPT‑2 outperforms models trained on domain-specific datasets (e.g. Wikipedia, news, books) when evaluated on those same datasets. The following table shows all our state-of-the-art zero-shot results.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><i><span>(+) means a higher score is better for this domain. (–) means a lower score is better.</span></i></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="max-w-container @container multi-columns:px-0 grid w-full grid-cols-12"><div class="full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4"><h5 class="text-h5-mobile @md:text-h5-desktop text-nowrap"></h5><div class="col-span-12 w-full overflow-auto"><div class="py-3xs @2xl:[&amp;_table]:table-fixed [&amp;_td]:p-3xs [&amp;_th]:p-4xs [&amp;_td]:min-w-3xl prose max-w-none [&amp;_table]:w-full w-[1px]"></div></div></div></div></div><div class="prose [&amp;_p]:text-caption [&amp;_p]:text-primary-60 col-span-12 max-w-none"><p>GPT‑2 achieves state-of-the-art on Winograd Schema, LAMBADA, and other language modeling tasks.</p></div></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>On other language tasks like question answering, reading comprehension, summarization, and translation, we are able to get surprising results without any fine-tuning of our models, simply by prompting the trained model in the right way (see below for examples of how we do this), though we do still fall short of state-of-the-art for specialized systems.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><section class="theme-light-gray @container grid grid-cols-12 w-full max-w-container max-w-[108rem]"><div class="col-span-12"><div role="status" class="max-w-container flex h-32 max-w-sm animate-pulse items-center justify-center rounded-lg bg-gray-300 dark:bg-gray-700"><span>Loading...</span></div></div></section><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We hypothesize that since these tasks are a subset of general language modeling, we can expect performance to increase further with more compute and data. Others have published </span><a href="https://arxiv.org/abs/1901.11373" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>similar hypotheses</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>. We also expect fine-tuning to help performance on downstream tasks, though we have yet to do thorough experiments.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="policy-implications"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Policy implications</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Large, general language models could have significant societal impacts, and also have many near-term applications. We can anticipate how systems like GPT‑2 could be used to create:</span></p><ul class="mb-md marker:text-inherit last:mb-0 list-disc pl-2xs mx-3xs"><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>AI writing assistants</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>More capable dialogue agents</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Unsupervised translation between languages</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Better speech recognition systems</span></li></ul><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We can also imagine the application of these models for </span><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" href="/index/preparing-for-malicious-uses-of-ai/"><span>malicious purposes</span>⁠</a><span>, including the following (or other applications we can’t yet anticipate):</span></p><ul class="mb-md marker:text-inherit last:mb-0 list-disc pl-2xs mx-3xs"><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Generate misleading news articles</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Impersonate others online</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Automate the production of abusive or faked content to post on social media</span></li><li class="mb-4xs last:mb-0"><span>Automate the production of spam/phishing content</span></li></ul><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>These findings, combined with earlier results on synthetic imagery, audio, and video, imply that technologies are reducing the cost of generating fake content and waging disinformation campaigns. The public at large will need to become more skeptical of text they find online, just as the “</span><a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3213954" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>deep fakes</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>” phenomenon calls for more skepticism about images.</span><sup><span id="citation-top-C"><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-primary-100 hover:text-primary-60 text-xs no-underline" href="#citation-bottom-C">C</a></span></sup></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Today, malicious actors—some of which are political in nature—have already begun to target the shared online commons, using </span><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/amphtml/opinions/global-opinions/the-new-censors-wont-delete-your-words--theyll-drown-them-out/2019/02/08/c8a926a2-2b27-11e9-984d-9b8fba003e81_story.html" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>things like</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> “robotic tools, fake accounts and dedicated teams to troll individuals with hateful commentary or smears that make them afraid to speak, or difficult to be heard or believed.” We should consider how research into the generation of synthetic images, videos, audio, and text may further combine to unlock new as-yet-unanticipated capabilities for these actors, and should seek to create better technical and non-technical countermeasures. Furthermore, the underlying technical innovations inherent to these systems are core to fundamental artificial intelligence research, so it is not possible to control research in these domains without slowing down the progress of AI as a whole.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="release-strategy"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Release strategy</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Due to concerns about large language models being used to generate deceptive, biased, or abusive language at scale, we are only releasing a </span><a href="https://github.com/openai/gpt-2/" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>much smaller version of GPT‑2 along with sampling code</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>. We are not releasing the dataset, training code, or GPT‑2 model weights. Nearly a year ago we wrote in the </span><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" href="/charter/"><span>OpenAI Charter</span>⁠</a><span>: “we expect that safety and security concerns will reduce our traditional publishing in the future, while increasing the importance of sharing safety, policy, and standards research,” and we see this current work as potentially representing the early beginnings of such concerns, which we expect may grow over time. This decision, as well as our discussion of it, is an experiment: while we are not sure that it is the right decision today, we believe that the AI community will eventually need to tackle the issue of publication norms in a thoughtful way in certain research areas. Other disciplines such as biotechnology and cybersecurity have long had active debates about responsible publication in cases with clear misuse potential, and we hope that our experiment will serve as a case study for more nuanced discussions of model and code release decisions in the AI community.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We are aware that some researchers have the technical capacity to reproduce and open source our results. We believe our release strategy limits the initial set of organizations who may choose to do this, and gives the AI community more time to have a discussion about the implications of such systems.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We also think governments should consider expanding or commencing initiatives to more systematically monitor the societal impact and diffusion of AI technologies, and to measure the progression in the capabilities of such systems. If pursued, these efforts could yield a better evidence base for decisions by AI labs and governments regarding publication decisions and AI policy more broadly.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We will further publicly discuss this strategy in six months. If you’d like to discuss large language models and their implications, please email us at: </span><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" href="mailto:languagequestions@openai.com"><span>languagequestions@openai.com</span>⁠</a><span>. And if you’re excited about working on cutting-edge language models (and thinking through their policy implications), </span><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" href="/careers/"><span>we’re hiring</span>⁠</a><span>.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><i><span>GPT‑2 Interim Update, May 2019</span></i></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We’re implementing two mechanisms to responsibly publish GPT‑2 and hopefully future releases: staged release and partnership-based sharing. We’re now </span><a href="https://github.com/openai/gpt-2" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>releasing</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> a larger 345M version of GPT‑2 as a next step in staged release, and are sharing the 762M and 1.5B versions with partners in the AI and security communities who are working to improve societal preparedness for large language models.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="staged-release"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Staged release</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>Staged release involves the gradual release of a family of models over time. The purpose of our staged release of GPT‑2 is to give people time to assess the properties of these models, discuss their societal implications, and evaluate the impacts of release after each stage.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>As the next step in our staged release strategy, we are releasing the 345M parameter version of GPT‑2. This model features improved performance relative to the 117M version, though falls short of the 1.5B version with respect to the ease of generating coherent text. We have been excited to see so many positive uses of GPT‑2-117M, and hope that 345M will yield still more benefits.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>While the misuse risk of 345M is higher than that of 117M, we believe it is substantially lower than that of 1.5B, and we believe that training systems of similar capability to GPT‑2-345M is well within the reach of many actors already; this evolving replication landscape has informed our decision-making about what is appropriate to release.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>In making our 345M release decision, some of the factors we considered include: the ease of use (by various users) of different model sizes for generating coherent text, the role of humans in the text generation process, the likelihood and timing of future replication and publication by others, evidence of use in the wild and expert-informed inferences about unobservable uses, proofs of concept such as the review generator mentioned in the original blog post, the strength of demand for the models for beneficial purposes, and the input of stakeholders and experts. We remain uncertain about some of these variables and continue to welcome input on how to make appropriate language model publication decisions.</span></p><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We hope that ongoing research on bias, detection, and misuse will give us the confidence to publish larger models in a timely manner, and at the six month mark we will share a fuller analysis of language models’ societal implications and our heuristics for release decisions.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="output-dataset"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Output dataset</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We’re </span><a href="https://github.com/openai/gpt-2-output-dataset" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>releasing</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> a dataset of GPT‑2 outputs from all 4 model sizes, with and without top-k truncation, as well as a subset of the WebText corpus used to train GPT‑2. The output dataset features approximately 250,000 samples per model/hyperparameter pair, which we expect is sufficient to help a wider range of researchers perform quantitative and qualitative analysis on the three topics above. Alongside these datasets, we are including a baseline analysis of some detection-related properties of the models, which we hope others will be able to quickly build on.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem] @md:-mb-[2.5rem] -mb-[1.75rem]"><!--$--><div class="@container max-w-container grid w-full grid-cols-12 toc-content-heading scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]" id="talk-to-us"><div class="@md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 col-span-12 max-w-none"><h2 class="text-h3 scroll-mt-[calc(var(--header-h)+var(--toc-button-h))]">Talk to us</h2></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class=""><!--$--><div class="w-full grid grid-cols-12 @container max-w-container multi-columns:px-0 multi-columns:flex"><div class="col-span-12 @md:col-span-6 @md:col-start-4 full-grid-content:@md:col-span-12 full-grid-content:@md:col-start-1 max-w-none prose"><p class="mb-sm last:mb-0"><span>We are interested in collaborating with researchers working on language model output detection, bias, and publication norms, and with organizations potentially affected by large language models: please reach out via our </span><a href="https://forms.gle/A7WBSbTY2EkKdroPA" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>Google Form</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span>. Additionally, OpenAI’s language, safety, and policy teams will be at </span><a href="https://iclr.cc/" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>ICLR</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> next week, including at the Reproducibility workshop and the OpenAI booth. In particular, we will be discussing this release strategy at the </span><a href="https://aiforsocialgood.github.io/iclr2019/schedule.htm" class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 underline-offset-[0.25rem] underline decoration-1 hover:text-primary-60 text-primary-100" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"><span>AI for Social Good</span>⁠<span class="sr-only">(opens in a new window)</span></a><span> workshop.</span></p></div></div><!--/$--></div><div class="@md:mt-[3.5rem] mt-[2rem]"><!--$--><section id="citations" data-testid="citations" class="max-w-container scroll-mt-header-h w-full"><div class="bg-primary-4 py-md md:py-xl px-xs grid grid-cols-12 rounded-md"><div class="gap-lg col-span-12 flex flex-col md:col-span-6 md:col-start-4"><section class="w-full"><ul class="gap-3xs flex flex-wrap"><li><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-nav px-3xs !py-4xs bg-primary-4 hover:bg-primary-12 block rounded-xl" href="/research/index/?tags=gpt">GPT</a></li><li><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-nav px-3xs !py-4xs bg-primary-4 hover:bg-primary-12 block rounded-xl" href="/research/index/?tags=language">Language</a></li><li><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-nav px-3xs !py-4xs bg-primary-4 hover:bg-primary-12 block rounded-xl" href="/research/index/?tags=generative-models">Generative Models</a></li><li><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-nav px-3xs !py-4xs bg-primary-4 hover:bg-primary-12 block rounded-xl" href="/research/index/?tags=ethics-safety">Ethics &amp; Safety</a></li><li><a class="transition ease-curve-a duration-250 text-nav px-3xs !py-4xs bg-primary-4 hover:bg-primary-12 block rounded-xl" href="/research/index/?tags=transformers">Transformers</a></li></ul></section><div data-testid="author-list"><h2 class="text-p2 text-primary-60 mb-3xs">Footnotes</h2><div class="prose max-w-none"><ol class="grid grid-cols-1 gap-y-3xs gap-x-sm px-0 !mb-0"><li id="citation-bottom-A" class="gap-x-4xs !mb-[.75rem] mt-0 inline-grid grid-cols-[auto,1fr] before:hidden"><span class="text-p2 text-primary-44 my-0 w-4">A</span><span class="mb-0"><p class="text-p2 [&amp;_*]:text-p2 mb-2xs break-words leading-none [word-break:break-word]"><span>We created a new dataset which emphasizes diversity of content, by scraping content from the Internet. In order to preserve document quality, we used only pages which have been curated/filtered by humans—specifically, we used outbound links from Reddit which received at least 3 karma. This can be thought of as a heuristic indicator for whether other users found the link interesting (whether educational or funny), leading to higher data quality than other similar datasets, such as penalties for the misuse of such systems, as some have proposed for deep fakes. </span><span class="inline-block"><button type="button" class="transition duration-200 ease-curve-a flex items-center
